

```python
import pandas as pd
from datetime import datetime
sf_file = "/home/sajit/coursera/ds_scale/systems_algos/assignments/datasci_course_materials/assignment6/sanfrancisco_incidents_summer_2014.csv"
sf = pd.read_csv(sf_file)
seattle_file = "/home/sajit/coursera/ds_scale/systems_algos/assignments/datasci_course_materials/assignment6/seattle_incidents_summer_2014.csv"
seattle = pd.read_csv(seattle_file)
seattle.columns = [c.replace(' ', '_') for c in seattle.columns]
```

# Basic data cleaning 

Both the datasets are quite different in the features so first let us arrange the data such that we can compare apples to apples. 


```python
def seattle_mapper(x):
    format =  '%m/%d/%Y %I:%M:%S %p'
    my_date = datetime.strptime(x,format)
    hour_slot = 0
    my_hour = my_date.hour
    if 6 <= my_hour < 12:
        hour_slot = 1
    elif 12 <= my_hour < 18:
        hour_slot = 2
    elif my_hour >= 18:
        hour_slot = 3
    return pd.Series({'time_of_day': hour_slot, 'day_of_week': my_date.weekday(), 'date': my_date.date()})

newcols = seattle['Occurred_Date_or_Date_Range_Start'].apply(seattle_mapper)

seattle = seattle.join(newcols)

seattle.columns.values

```

```python
def mapper_sf_time(x):
    hour = int(x.split(':')[0])
    if 0<= hour < 6:
        return 0;
    elif 6<= hour < 12:
        return 1;
    elif 12 <= hour < 18:
        return 2;
    else:
        return 3

def sf_map_date(x):
    format = '%m/%d/%Y'
    my_date = datetime.strptime(x,format)
    return my_date.month



def mapper_dayofweek(x):
    if x == 'Sunday':
        return 6;
    elif x == 'Monday':
        return 0;
    elif x == 'Tuesday':
        return 1;
    elif x == 'Wednesday':
        return  2;
    elif x == 'Thursday':
        return 3;
    elif x == 'Friday':
        return 4;
    elif x == 'Saturday':
        return 5;
    else:
        ArithmeticError

sf['day_of_week'] = sf['DayOfWeek'].apply(mapper_dayofweek)
sf['Month'] = sf['Date'].apply(sf_map_date)
sf['time_of_day'] = sf['Time'].apply(mapper_sf_time)

sf.columns.values


```

